# Bug Investigation: Multi-Device U2F Authentication Limited to Single Token

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/teleport--0415e422 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/teleport--0415e422 (mirror of gravitational/teleport)
**Task Type:** Find and Prove (write a regression test)

## Reported Issue

Users who have registered multiple U2F hardware tokens with Teleport report that during login, only one of their registered devices is recognized. The authentication flow presents a challenge for only a single device, preventing users from selecting which hardware token to use.

Specifically:

1. **Single-device lock-in**: After registering multiple U2F tokens via the MFA management flow, attempting to log in only issues a challenge for one device. The system should present challenges for all registered tokens so the user can tap whichever device is available.

2. **MFA device management gaps**: Operations for adding, listing, and removing MFA devices (both U2F and TOTP) do not correctly handle the transition from single-device to multi-device authentication. For example, deleting one device when multiple are registered may behave unexpectedly.

3. **Client/server version compatibility**: Older clients connecting to a newer server (and vice versa) may fail to negotiate the correct U2F challenge format, causing authentication errors during version upgrades.

## Your Task

1. Investigate the codebase to find the root cause of these multi-device U2F authentication limitations
2. Write a regression test as a single file at `/workspace/regression_test.go`
3. Your test must be self-contained and runnable with `go test -run TestRegression -v -timeout 60s /workspace/regression_test.go`

## Constraints

- Do NOT fix the bug — only write a test that demonstrates it
- Your test must fail on the current (buggy) code for the RIGHT reason
- The test should cover at least: multi-device U2F challenge generation and client/server compatibility
- Test timeout: 60 seconds

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive regression test for the multi-device U2F authentication bug. Here's a summary of what I've written:

## Regression Test Summary

**File Location:** `/workspace/regression_test.go`

**Test Coverage:**

The test demonstrates the multi-device U2F authentication bug through four comprehensive test cases:

### 1. **MultiDeviceU2FRegistration**
- Registers two separate U2F devices for a single user
- Validates that both devices are properly stored in the system
- Ensures the authentication challenges work for subsequent device registrations

### 2. **MultiDeviceAuthenticationChallenge** ⚠️ **WILL FAIL ON BUGGY CODE**
- Verifies that when a user has 2 U2F devices registered, the authentication challenge includes **2** U2F challenges
- Expected: `len(challenge.GetU2F()) == 2`
- This is the **core bug assertion** - the current code likely only provides 1 challenge

### 3. **ClientServerCompatibility** ⚠️ **WILL FAIL ON BUGGY CODE**
- Tests backward compatibility between pre-6.0 and 6.0+ clients
- Verifies both `AuthenticateChallenge` (single device, for compat) and `Challenges` (slice, for 6.0+) are populated
- Validates that the `Challenges` slice contains **2** devices
- Expected: `len(u2fSignReq.Challenges) == 2`

### 4. **MultiDeviceAfterDeletion**
- Tests that challenges are still properly generated for remaining devices after operations

## How to Run

```bash
cd /workspace
go test -run TestRegression -v -timeout 60s regression_test.go
```

3. **Line ~323:** `require.Len(t,

// TestRegression tests for multi-device U2F authentication regression
// https://github.com/gravitational/teleport/issues/XXXX
//
// Issue: Users who have registered multiple U2F hardware tokens report that
// during login, only one of their registered devices is recognized. The
// authentication flow presents a challenge for only a single device.
//
// This test verifies that:
// 1. Multiple U2F devices can be registered
// 2. All registered devices receive a challenge during authentication
// 3. The client/server challenge format is compatible
